All consumer instances\\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\\n98:  * <p>\\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n49: \n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n51: \n52: /**\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n54:  * <p>\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n58:  * <p>\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n62:  *\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n68:  * <p>\n69:  *\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n79:  * <p>\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n88:  * <p>\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n90:  * detail below.\n91:  *\n92:  * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n93:  *\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n95:  * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n96:  * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n98:  * <p>\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java%3FL1-100"}}}

Modern Implementation\\n\\n### Overview\\nThe Apache Kafka codebase has evolved from a legacy `ConsumerConnector` interface to the modern `KafkaConsumer` API, which now supports multiple consumer group protocols (classic and new) through an internal delegation pattern.\\n\\n### Core Implementation Files\\n\\n#### Kafka Repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)\\n\\n**New KafkaConsumer API Architecture:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java**: The main public consumer facade that delegates to either ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer based on group protocol configuration (KIP-848). This is the primary entry point for all consumer operations.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java**: Internal interface extending the Consumer interface, providing methods for internal use (clientId(), metricsRegistry(), kafkaConsumerMetrics(), updateAssignmentMetadataIfNeeded()).\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java**: Factory class that inspects ConsumerConfig.GROUP_PROTOCOL_CONFIG and creates either AsyncKafkaConsumer (for 'consumer' protocol) or ClassicKafkaConsumer (for legacy/classic protocol).\\n\\n**Legacy Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848). Contains synchronous implementation using ConsumerCoordinator for group coordination and offset management. This is the backward-compatible implementation.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java**: Manages group coordination and offset commits for ClassicKafkaConsumer. Key offset management methods:\\n  - commitOffsetsSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, Timer): Synchronously commits offsets\\n  - commitOffsetsAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback): Asynchronously commits offsets\\n  - Tracks in-flight async commits and invokes callbacks upon completion\\n\\n**New Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848). Uses event-based architecture with dedicated request managers for handling network I/O asynchronously.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java**: Manages offset commits in AsyncKafkaConsumer using an event-driven approach. Features:\\n  - Uses PendingRequests queue for managing commit requests\\n  - Supports both sync and async commits through events (SyncCommitEvent, AsyncCommitEvent)\\n  - Implements AutoCommitState for periodic automatic offset commits\\n  - Integrates with CoordinatorRequestManager for group coordination\\n\\n**Offset Management Infrastructure:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java**: Handles fetching committed offsets from brokers. Used by ClassicKafkaConsumer for offset initialization and recovery.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java**: Data class representing an offset with associated metadata, used throughout both implementations for offset commit/fetch operations.\\n\\n### Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n**ClassicKafkaConsumer (Legacy Group Protocol):**\\n1. **Synchronous Architecture**: All network operations are blocking, occurring in the application thread\\n2. **ConsumerCoordinator Managed**: Single coordinator handles both group membership and offset management\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Direct API calls to commitSync() and commitAsync() trigger immediate offset commit requests\\n4. **Callback Model**: Uses OffsetCommitCallback for async completion notification\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Synchronous rebalance listeners invoked on application thread\\n\\n**AsyncKafkaConsumer (New Group Protocol - KIP-848):**\\n1. **Event-Driven Architecture**: Network operations use event-based, asynchronous model with background threads\\n2. **Separated Concerns**: CommitRequestManager handles offset commits separately from CoordinatorRequestManager (group coordination)\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Commit requests are enqueued as events (SyncCommitEvent/AsyncCommitEvent) for background processing\\n4. **CompletableFuture Model**: Async operations return CompletableFuture instead of using callbacks\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Asynchronous rebalance listener invocation with proper event sequencing\\n\\n### Integration Points\\n\\n#### Camel Kafka Component (sg-evals/camel--1006f047)\\n\\nCamel integrates with the modern KafkaConsumer API through:\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java**: Camel's consumer wrapper around org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.Consumer interface\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaFetchRecords.java**: Fetches records using the underlying Kafka consumer and manages offset state\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java**: Factory that instantiates org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer\\n- **Commit Managers**: \\n  - **SyncCommitManager.java**: Performs synchronous offset commits via consumer.commitSync()\\n  - **AsyncCommitManager.java**: Performs asynchronous offset commits via consumer.commitAsync()\\n  - **CommitManagers.java**: Factory that selects the appropriate commit manager based on configuration\\n\\n#### Flink Kafka Connector (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc)\\n\\n- **flink-python/pyflink/datastream/connectors/kafka.py**: FlinkKafkaConsumer is deprecated in favor of KafkaSource. This represents the legacy wrapper approach that has been superseded by modern source implementations.\\n\\n### Migration Path Summary\\n\\n1. **Old API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector)**: Deprecated and removed in Kafka 4.0, used pre-KIP-848\\n2. **Current KafkaConsumer with ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains backward compatibility with classic group protocol\\n3. **Modern AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Implements new KIP-848 protocol with event-driven architecture\\n4. **Consumer abstraction level**: All implementations use Consumer interface at abstraction boundary (as seen in Camel)\\n\\nThe migration preserves backward compatibility while enabling more efficient, event-driven consumer implementations through the delegation pattern, allowing applications to seamlessly upgrade to the new protocol without changing their code.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1721,"cache_read_input_tokens":94762,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1721},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"51d43bd9-1100-4876-99c4-1bbe259507e6","uuid":"da3b0ead-3ae7-4f73-a937-482b9189e4c1"}

Modern Implementation\\n\\n### Overview\\nThe Apache Kafka codebase has evolved from a legacy `ConsumerConnector` interface to the modern `KafkaConsumer` API, which now supports multiple consumer group protocols (classic and new) through an internal delegation pattern.\\n\\n### Core Implementation Files\\n\\n#### Kafka Repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)\\n\\n**New KafkaConsumer API Architecture:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java**: The main public consumer facade that delegates to either ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer based on group protocol configuration (KIP-848). This is the primary entry point for all consumer operations.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java**: Internal interface extending the Consumer interface, providing methods for internal use (clientId(), metricsRegistry(), kafkaConsumerMetrics(), updateAssignmentMetadataIfNeeded()).\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java**: Factory class that inspects ConsumerConfig.GROUP_PROTOCOL_CONFIG and creates either AsyncKafkaConsumer (for 'consumer' protocol) or ClassicKafkaConsumer (for legacy/classic protocol).\\n\\n**Legacy Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848). Contains synchronous implementation using ConsumerCoordinator for group coordination and offset management. This is the backward-compatible implementation.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java**: Manages group coordination and offset commits for ClassicKafkaConsumer. Key offset management methods:\\n  - commitOffsetsSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, Timer): Synchronously commits offsets\\n  - commitOffsetsAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback): Asynchronously commits offsets\\n  - Tracks in-flight async commits and invokes callbacks upon completion\\n\\n**New Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848). Uses event-based architecture with dedicated request managers for handling network I/O asynchronously.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java**: Manages offset commits in AsyncKafkaConsumer using an event-driven approach. Features:\\n  - Uses PendingRequests queue for managing commit requests\\n  - Supports both sync and async commits through events (SyncCommitEvent, AsyncCommitEvent)\\n  - Implements AutoCommitState for periodic automatic offset commits\\n  - Integrates with CoordinatorRequestManager for group coordination\\n\\n**Offset Management Infrastructure:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java**: Handles fetching committed offsets from brokers. Used by ClassicKafkaConsumer for offset initialization and recovery.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java**: Data class representing an offset with associated metadata, used throughout both implementations for offset commit/fetch operations.\\n\\n### Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n**ClassicKafkaConsumer (Legacy Group Protocol):**\\n1. **Synchronous Architecture**: All network operations are blocking, occurring in the application thread\\n2. **ConsumerCoordinator Managed**: Single coordinator handles both group membership and offset management\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Direct API calls to commitSync() and commitAsync() trigger immediate offset commit requests\\n4. **Callback Model**: Uses OffsetCommitCallback for async completion notification\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Synchronous rebalance listeners invoked on application thread\\n\\n**AsyncKafkaConsumer (New Group Protocol - KIP-848):**\\n1. **Event-Driven Architecture**: Network operations use event-based, asynchronous model with background threads\\n2. **Separated Concerns**: CommitRequestManager handles offset commits separately from CoordinatorRequestManager (group coordination)\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Commit requests are enqueued as events (SyncCommitEvent/AsyncCommitEvent) for background processing\\n4. **CompletableFuture Model**: Async operations return CompletableFuture instead of using callbacks\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Asynchronous rebalance listener invocation with proper event sequencing\\n\\n### Integration Points\\n\\n#### Camel Kafka Component (sg-evals/camel--1006f047)\\n\\nCamel integrates with the modern KafkaConsumer API through:\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java**: Camel's consumer wrapper around org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.Consumer interface\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaFetchRecords.java**: Fetches records using the underlying Kafka consumer and manages offset state\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java**: Factory that instantiates org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer\\n- **Commit Managers**: \\n  - **SyncCommitManager.java**: Performs synchronous offset commits via consumer.commitSync()\\n  - **AsyncCommitManager.java**: Performs asynchronous offset commits via consumer.commitAsync()\\n  - **CommitManagers.java**: Factory that selects the appropriate commit manager based on configuration\\n\\n#### Flink Kafka Connector (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc)\\n\\n- **flink-python/pyflink/datastream/connectors/kafka.py**: FlinkKafkaConsumer is deprecated in favor of KafkaSource. This represents the legacy wrapper approach that has been superseded by modern source implementations.\\n\\n### Migration Path Summary\\n\\n1. **Old API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector)**: Deprecated and removed in Kafka 4.0, used pre-KIP-848\\n2. **Current KafkaConsumer with ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains backward compatibility with classic group protocol\\n3. **Modern AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Implements new KIP-848 protocol with event-driven architecture\\n4. **Consumer abstraction level**: All implementations use Consumer interface at abstraction boundary (as seen in Camel)\\n\\nThe migration preserves backward compatibility while enabling more efficient, event-driven consumer implementations through the delegation pattern, allowing applications to seamlessly upgrade to the new protocol without changing their code.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
